Thanks! Here’s the plan and what I’ve implemented:

- Scaffold minimal Python projects for mcp-server and mcp-client without external dependencies.
- Implement a local HTTP server that exposes a Jira issues endpoint.
- Add a CLI client that calls the server and prints issues.
- Integrate Jira API using only Python standard library (`urllib`, `http.server`, `ssl`).
- Provide env-based config and a mock mode to avoid real Jira calls.
- Add READMEs with PowerShell run steps and a smoke test script.

**What’s Included**
- __main__.py: HTTP server at `http://127.0.0.1:8765` with `GET /jira/issues?project=<KEY>&maxResults=<N>`. Reads `JIRA_BASE_URL`, `JIRA_EMAIL`, `JIRA_API_TOKEN`; mock mode via `JIRA_MOCK=1`.
- __main__.py: CLI that calls the server and prints `KEY | STATUS | SUMMARY`.
- .env.example: Example env vars (server reads actual environment; no .env parsing).
- README.md and README.md: PowerShell-friendly usage.
- smoke_test.ps1: Starts server in mock mode and queries sample project.

**Try It (PowerShell)**
- Run the server:
```powershell
$env:JIRA_BASE_URL = "https://your-domain.atlassian.net"
$env:JIRA_EMAIL = "you@example.com"
$env:JIRA_API_TOKEN = "your_api_token"
# For mock mode:
# $env:JIRA_MOCK = "1"

python -m mcp_server
```

- Run the client (in another terminal):
```powershell
python -m mcp_client --project ABC --max 5
```

- Quick mock smoke test:
```powershell
cd c:\Users\v776133\Downloads\JiraAgent\mcp-client
.\smoke_test.ps1
```

**Notes**
- No external package installs used; everything relies on Python stdlib.
- Jira API auth uses Basic with email + API token; ensure your Jira site and token are correct.
- If env vars aren’t set, the server returns mock data to keep local development frictionless.

**About `.env.example`**
- The app does not read `.env` files automatically. The `.env.example` is a reference.
- Use PowerShell env vars as shown, or set persistent system environment variables via Windows:
  - Open “System Properties” → “Environment Variables…”
  - Add `JIRA_BASE_URL`, `JIRA_EMAIL`, `JIRA_API_TOKEN` (and optionally `JIRA_MOCK`) under your user variables.
  - Restart PowerShell windows to pick up changes.

marieswari-palanimarimuthu_verizon: How can i get api token

GitHub Copilot: Acknowledged. I’ll outline how to obtain a Jira API token and cover both Atlassian Cloud and on‑prem cases.

**Atlassian Cloud (your-domain.atlassian.net)**
- **Navigate:** Go to `https://id.atlassian.com/manage-profile/security/api-tokens`.
- **Create token:** Click “Create API token”, add a label, then “Create”.
- **Copy token:** Copy the generated token and store it securely.
- **Use in env:** Set `JIRA_EMAIL` to your Atlassian account email and `JIRA_API_TOKEN` to the copied token.

**PowerShell Setup**
```powershell
$env:JIRA_BASE_URL = "https://your-domain.atlassian.net"
$env:JIRA_EMAIL = "you@example.com"
$env:JIRA_API_TOKEN = "paste_token_here"
python -m mcp_server
```

**On‑Prem Jira (e.g., onejira.verizon.com)**
- **Check support:** On‑prem Jira may not use Atlassian Cloud API tokens.
- **Options:**
  - If your instance supports **Personal Access Tokens (PATs)**: go to your profile → “Personal Access Tokens” (path varies by version/add-ons), create a token, then use it as `JIRA_API_TOKEN` with your email/username.
  - If PATs are not available: Basic auth may require your **username + password** (confirm with your security policy; password auth to API is often disabled).
- **Set API version:** On on‑prem, use REST API v2:
```powershell
$env:JIRA_BASE_URL = "https://onejira.verizon.com"
$env:JIRA_API_VERSION = "2"
$env:JIRA_EMAIL = "your.enterprise.email@verizon.com"
$env:JIRA_API_TOKEN = "your_PAT_or_password_if_allowed"
python -m mcp_server
```

**Tips**
- **2FA enabled:** API tokens bypass 2FA; passwords typically won’t work with 2FA for Cloud.
- **Least privilege:** Scope tokens minimally if PATs support scoping.
- **Rotate regularly:** Revoke and recreate tokens periodically.
- **Test quickly:** If calls fail, try switching `JIRA_API_VERSION` between `2` and `3`, and verify your base URL.

Great question. I’ve updated the server and client so you can pull defects assigned to you in a specific project using simple flags.

- Server now supports filters via query params: `assignedTo`, `type`, and `status`. It builds JQL like: project="Your Project" AND assignee=currentUser() AND issuetype="Bug" AND status="Open".
- Client adds flags: `--assigned me`, `--type Bug`, `--status Open`.

Try this:

- Start the server:
```powershell

# $env:JIRA_MOCK = "1"

```

- Pull defects assigned to you:
```powershell

python -m mcp_client --project "B6VV_CXP Operations" --assigned me --type Bug --status Open --max 25
```

Notes:
- If your project is a key without spaces (e.g., `B6VV_CXP`), you can use `--project B6VV_CXP`.
- You can omit `--status` to see all statuses, or change `--type` if your instance uses “Defect” instead of “Bug”.

marieswari-palanimarimuthu_verizon: How to check  JIRA_MOCK is not set.

GitHub Copilot: Acknowledged. I’ll share quick PowerShell checks and how to unset it.

- Check current value:
```powershell
Get-Item Env:JIRA_MOCK
```
If it returns nothing, it’s not set. If it shows `Name: JIRA_MOCK  Value: 1`, mock mode is on.

- Check with a default fallback:
```powershell
$val = $env:JIRA_MOCK; if ($null -eq $val) { "JIRA_MOCK not set" } else { "JIRA_MOCK=$val" }
```

- Unset (turn off mock mode) for the current session:
```powershell
Remove-Item Env:JIRA_MOCK -ErrorAction SilentlyContinue
```

- Verify it’s gone:
```powershell
Get-Item Env:JIRA_MOCK
```

Run these in the same terminal where you start the server (`python -m mcp_server`), as environment variables are per process/session.

marieswari-palanimarimuthu_verizon: where can i find $env:JIRA_API_VERSION = "2" in https://onejira.verizon.com/

GitHub Copilot: Good question. `JIRA_API_VERSION` is not something you “find” on the website; it’s an environment variable we use to tell our server which Jira REST API path to call. On Atlassian Cloud, v3 is standard. On many on‑prem/server/Data Center instances (like `onejira.verizon.com`), v2 is typical.

Here’s how to verify which API version your instance supports:

- Check server info endpoints:
```powershell
# v2 (Jira Server/Data Center usually supports this)
Invoke-WebRequest -Uri "https://onejira.verizon.com/rest/api/2/serverInfo" -UseBasicParsing

# v3 (Cloud standard; some on-prem may proxy this but often don’t)
Invoke-WebRequest -Uri "https://onejira.verizon.com/rest/api/3/serverInfo" -UseBasicParsing
```
- Expected: One of these returns 200 with JSON. If `/rest/api/2/…` works and `/rest/api/3/…` fails, use `JIRA_API_VERSION = "2"`.

To test the search endpoint quickly with your credentials:
```powershell
# Replace with your email and token/PAT (or password if your instance requires it)
$Email = "your.enterprise.email@verizon.com"
$Token = "your_token_or_password"

# Basic auth header
$pair = [System.Text.Encoding]::UTF8.GetBytes("$Email:$Token")
$auth = [Convert]::ToBase64String($pair)

# Try v2 search
$uri2 = "https://onejira.verizon.com/rest/api/2/search?jql=project=""B6VV_CXP Operations""&maxResults=1"
Invoke-WebRequest -Uri $uri2 -Headers @{ Authorization = "Basic $auth"; Accept = "application/json" } -UseBasicParsing

# Try v3 search
$uri3 = "https://onejira.verizon.com/rest/api/3/search?jql=project=""B6VV_CXP Operations""&maxResults=1"
Invoke-WebRequest -Uri $uri3 -Headers @{ Authorization = "Basic $auth"; Accept = "application/json" } -UseBasicParsing
```

- If v2 works, set in the server terminal before starting it:
```powershell
$env:JIRA_BASE_URL = "https://onejira.verizon.com"
$env:JIRA_API_VERSION = "2"
$env:JIRA_EMAIL = "your.enterprise.email@verizon.com"
$env:JIRA_API_TOKEN = "your_token_or_password"
python -m mcp_server
```

Notes:
- Authentication on on‑prem varies: some instances use personal access tokens, some allow username+password for API, and some require app links or SSO app passwords. If 401/403 occurs, confirm your org’s approved method.
- Once the server is running, the console will print the JQL and the exact URL it’s calling, so you can confirm it’s using `/rest/api/2/search`.

If you want, I can add a small PowerShell script (`verify_api_version.ps1`) that probes both endpoints and tells you which one works, then sets `JIRA_API_VERSION` accordingly.

GitHub Copilot: Thanks for the update — the 401 confirms Jira is rejecting the credentials the server is sending. Let’s zero in on on‑prem auth specifics and verify with a direct test so we know exactly what Jira expects.

**Plan**
- Verify whether your Jira accepts username+password or Personal Access Token (PAT).
- Test direct REST call using Basic auth with `JIRA_USERNAME` and your password/PAT.

**Direct Auth Test (bypassing our server)**
Run this from PowerShell to hit Jira’s v2 search with Basic auth using your username:

```powershell
# Set your Jira username and either your Jira password or PAT (whichever your org supports)
$Username = "v776133"
$Secret   = "<your Jira password or PAT>"

# Build Basic auth header
$bytes = [System.Text.Encoding]::UTF8.GetBytes("$Username:$Secret")
$auth  = [Convert]::ToBase64String($bytes)

# Minimal JQL just to test auth; project-only
$uri = "https://onejira.verizon.com/rest/api/2/search?jql=project=""B6VV_CXP Operations""&maxResults=1"

# Call Jira directly
Invoke-WebRequest -Uri $uri -Headers @{ Authorization = "Basic $auth"; Accept = "application/json" } -UseBasicParsing
```

- If this returns 200 with JSON, you’ve confirmed the correct credential type and format.
- If it returns 401, then the chosen secret isn’t accepted; try:
  - Your Jira password (if policy allows API basic with password).
  - A Personal Access Token from your Jira profile (if available).
  - If PAT isn’t available, ask your Jira admin for the approved API auth (some orgs require app passwords or session cookies via login endpoint).

marieswari-palanimarimuthu_verizon: How to run direct jira test in single execution to avoid issues in username and secret

GitHub Copilot: Good idea. Here’s a single, copy‑paste PowerShell block that safely handles username/secret interpolation and quoting, runs the direct Jira test, and prints a clear result.

```powershell
# --- Direct Jira Auth Test (single execution) ---
$Username = "v776133"
$Secret   = "<YOUR_PAT_OR_PASSWORD>"   # paste your PAT or Jira password

# Build Basic auth header safely using ${} interpolation
$bytes = [System.Text.Encoding]::UTF8.GetBytes("${Username}:${Secret}")
$auth  = [Convert]::ToBase64String($bytes)

# Target: Jira Server/Data Center REST API v2
$Project = 'B6VV_CXP Operations'
$Jql     = 'project="' + $Project + '"'
$Uri     = 'https://onejira.verizon.com/rest/api/2/search?jql=' + [uri]::EscapeDataString($Jql) + '&maxResults=1'

Write-Host "Testing Jira auth against:" $Uri

try {
    $resp = Invoke-WebRequest -Uri $Uri -Headers @{ Authorization = "Basic $auth"; Accept = "application/json" } -UseBasicParsing
    if ($resp.StatusCode -eq 200) {
        Write-Host "PASS: Auth succeeded. Received JSON." -ForegroundColor Green
        # Show minimal snippet
        $json = $resp.Content
        Write-Host ($json.Substring(0, [Math]::Min($json.Length, 300))) "..."
    } else {
        Write-Host "WARN: Received status code: $($resp.StatusCode)" -ForegroundColor Yellow
    }
} catch {
    Write-Host "FAIL: $($_.Exception.Message)" -ForegroundColor Red
    if ($_.Exception.Response -and $_.Exception.Response.StatusCode) {
        Write-Host "HTTP Status: $([int]$_.Exception.Response.StatusCode)"
    }
}
# --- End ---
```

Notes:
- Replace `<YOUR_PAT_OR_PASSWORD>` with your actual PAT or Jira password.
- This uses REST API v2 (`/rest/api/2/...`), which your instance supports.
- It escapes JQL properly and avoids the `$Username:$Secret` colon parsing issue.
- On success, you’ll see “PASS” and a snippet of JSON. On failure, you’ll get a clear “FAIL” with HTTP status.

If this passes, set the same values in the server env and restart:
```powershell
$env:JIRA_BASE_URL = "https://onejira.verizon.com"
$env:JIRA_API_VERSION = "2"
$env:JIRA_USERNAME = $Username
$env:JIRA_API_TOKEN = $Secret
Remove-Item Env:JIRA_MOCK -ErrorAction SilentlyContinue

cd C:\Users\v776133\Downloads\JiraAgent\mcp-server
python -m mcp_server
```

GitHub Copilot: Acknowledged. Here’s a single, copy‑paste PowerShell block that runs end-to-end in one execution, with safe interpolation and quoting:

```powershell
# --- Single execution: fetch rendered comments for an issue ---
$Username = "v776133"
$Secret   = "PegaManager2$"  # your Jira password (or PAT if supported)

# Build Basic auth header safely
$bytes = [System.Text.Encoding]::UTF8.GetBytes("${Username}:${Secret}")
$auth  = [Convert]::ToBase64String($bytes)

# API v2 (Server/Data Center) with renderedBody
$IssueKey = "CXPOPER-46300"
$Uri      = "https://onejira.verizon.com/rest/api/2/issue/$IssueKey/comment?expand=renderedBody&orderBy=created&maxResults=50"

Write-Host "Calling: $Uri"
try {
    $resp = Invoke-WebRequest -Uri $Uri -Headers @{ Authorization = "Basic $auth"; Accept = "application/json" } -UseBasicParsing
    if ($resp.StatusCode -eq 200) {
        $json = $resp.Content | ConvertFrom-Json
        $comments = $json.comments
        if (-not $comments -or $comments.Count -eq 0) {
            Write-Host "No comments found."
        } else {
            # Sort by created; pick latest
            $latest = $comments | Sort-Object created | Select-Object -Last 1
            $author = if ($latest.author.displayName) { $latest.author.displayName } elseif ($latest.author.name) { $latest.author.name } else { "" }
            $created = $latest.created
            $bodyPlain = $latest.body
            $bodyHtml  = $latest.renderedBody  # may be null if not available

            Write-Host ("{0} | {1} | {2}" -f $IssueKey, $author, $created)
            if ($bodyHtml) {
                Write-Host "Rendered HTML:"
                $bodyHtml
            } else {
                Write-Host "Plain body:"
                $bodyPlain
            }
        }
    } else {
        Write-Host "WARN: Status $($resp.StatusCode)"
        $resp.Content
    }
} catch {
    Write-Host "FAIL: $($_.Exception.Message)"
    if ($_.Exception.Response -and $_.Exception.Response.StatusCode) {
        Write-Host "HTTP Status: $([int]$_.Exception.Response.StatusCode)"
    }
}
# --- End ---
```

- Uses `renderedBody` for richer HTML when available; falls back to plain `body`.
- Replace `Secret` with your Jira password or PAT (if PATs are supported on your instance).
- You can change `$IssueKey` to any other defect key.

Quick diagnostics you can run

```powershell
# From C:\Users\v776133\Downloads\JiraAgent\mcp-server
```

- Try calling the endpoint directly to see raw error payload:
```powershell
$project = 'B6VV_CXP Operations'  # or your exact project name
```

Common causes of 500 here
- Project name quoting: We already quote it in JQL, including spaces. If the project name casing or exact label differs, try the project key instead.
- Auth mismatch: Your `/debug/env` looks correct (OneJira v2; username/password in `JIRA_API_TOKEN_set`). If you’re using email+token on-prem, switch to `JIRA_USERNAME` + password.
- Field enrichment: We added `expand=names` and map components and custom fields. If a null field is accessed, the server should still handle it, but the detailed error will confirm.

marieswari-palanimarimuthu_verizon: How to execute as a single execution

GitHub Copilot: Here are concise single-line PowerShell options, using semicolons to chain commands.

- Start the MCP server with envs in one go:
```powershell
$env:JIRA_BASE_URL='https://onejira.verizon.com'; $env:JIRA_API_VERSION='2'; $env:JIRA_USERNAME='<your_username>'; $env:JIRA_API_TOKEN='<your_password>'; $env:JIRA_MOCK='0'; python -m mcp_server
```

- Start the server in background, then hit `/jira/issues`:
```powershell
$env:JIRA_BASE_URL='https://onejira.verizon.com'; $env:JIRA_API_VERSION='2'; $env:JIRA_USERNAME='<your_username>'; $env:JIRA_API_TOKEN='<your_password>'; $env:JIRA_MOCK='0'; Start-Process -FilePath python -ArgumentList '-m','mcp_server'; Start-Sleep -Seconds 1; Invoke-WebRequest -Uri 'http://127.0.0.1:8765/jira/issues?project=B6VV_CXP%20Operations&maxResults=25' | Select-Object -ExpandProperty Content
```

- Single shot: direct Jira latest comment fetch (no server), printing rendered HTML if present:
```powershell
$IssueKey='CXPOPER-46300'; $User='<your_username>'; $Pass='<your_password>'; $auth=[Convert]::ToBase64String([Text.Encoding]::ASCII.GetBytes("${User}:${Pass}")); $Uri=\"https://onejira.verizon.com/rest/api/2/issue/$IssueKey/comment?orderBy=created&maxResults=50&expand=renderedBody\"; $resp=Invoke-WebRequest -Uri $Uri -Headers @{Authorization=\"Basic $auth\";Accept='application/json'} -UseBasicParsing; $json=$resp.Content|ConvertFrom-Json; $c=$json.comments|Sort-Object created|Select-Object -Last 1; Write-Host (\"{0} | {1} | {2}\" -f $IssueKey, ($c.author.displayName ?? $c.author.name), $c.created); if ($c.renderedBody) { $c.renderedBody } else { $c.body }
```

- One-liner UI launch:
```powershell
Start-Process "C:\Users\v776133\Downloads\JiraAgent\mcp-client\ui\index.html"
```

If you want a single command that sets envs, starts server, and opens the UI, we can wrap it into a `.ps1` script or a chained command using `Start-Process` twice. Want me to generate that script?

marieswari-palanimarimuthu_verizon: How to run as a single execution in powershell $project = 'B6VV_CXP Operations'  # or your exact project name

GitHub Copilot: Here’s your three-line PowerShell snippet collapsed into a single execution, using semicolons:

```powershell
$project='B6VV_CXP Operations'; $qs=[System.Web.HttpUtility]::UrlEncode("project=$project&maxResults=25"); Invoke-WebRequest -Uri "http://127.0.0.1:8765/jira/issues?$qs" -UseBasicParsing | Select-Object -ExpandProperty Content
```

Examples with optional filters (comma-separated lists supported):
- Add Status list:
```powershell
$project='B6VV_CXP Operations'; $status='Open,In Progress'; $qs=[System.Web.HttpUtility]::UrlEncode("project=$project&status=$status&maxResults=25"); Invoke-WebRequest -Uri "http://127.0.0.1:8765/jira/issues?$qs" -UseBasicParsing | Select-Object -ExpandProperty Content
```
- Add Priority list:
```powershell
$project='B6VV_CXP Operations'; $priority='High,Medium'; $qs=[System.Web.HttpUtility]::UrlEncode("project=$project&priority=$priority&maxResults=25"); Invoke-WebRequest -Uri "http://127.0.0.1:8765/jira/issues?$qs" -UseBasicParsing | Select-Object -ExpandProperty Content
```
- With assignee “me”:
```powershell
$project='B6VV_CXP Operations'; $qs=[System.Web.HttpUtility]::UrlEncode("project=$project&assignedTo=me&maxResults=25"); Invoke-WebRequest -Uri "http://127.0.0.1:8765/jira/issues?$qs" -UseBasicParsing | Select-Object -ExpandProperty Content
```

Tip: Ensure the server is running first (`python -m mcp_server`).

GitHub Copilot: You’re hitting two issues: `System.Web.HttpUtility` isn’t available, and the server rejects the request because `project` wasn’t sent.

Use `[uri]::EscapeDataString` to build the query string in PowerShell 5.1, all in one line:

- Minimal (project only):
```powershell
$project='B6VV_CXP Operations'; $qs="project=$([uri]::EscapeDataString($project))&maxResults=25"; Invoke-WebRequest -Uri "http://127.0.0.1:8765/jira/issues?$qs" -UseBasicParsing | Select-Object -ExpandProperty Content
```

- With Status list:
```powershell
$project='B6VV_CXP Operations'; $status='Open,In Progress'; $qs="project=$([uri]::EscapeDataString($project))&status=$([uri]::EscapeDataString($status))&maxResults=25"; Invoke-WebRequest -Uri "http://127.0.0.1:8765/jira/issues?$qs" -UseBasicParsing | Select-Object -ExpandProperty Content
```

- With Priority list:
```powershell
$project='B6VV_CXP Operations'; $priority='High,Medium'; $qs="project=$([uri]::EscapeDataString($project))&priority=$([uri]::EscapeDataString($priority))&maxResults=25"; Invoke-WebRequest -Uri "http://127.0.0.1:8765/jira/issues?$qs" -UseBasicParsing | Select-Object -ExpandProperty Content
```

- With assignee “me”:
```powershell
$project='B6VV_CXP Operations'; $qs="project=$([uri]::EscapeDataString($project))&assignedTo=me&maxResults=25"; Invoke-WebRequest -Uri "http://127.0.0.1:8765/jira/issues?$qs" -UseBasicParsing | Select-Object -ExpandProperty Content
```

Make sure the server is running first:
```powershell
python -m mcp_server
```

marieswari-palanimarimuthu_verizon: Which LLM can be used in jiraagent to make it efficient and productive ?

GitHub Copilot: Acknowledged. High-level plan: outline practical LLM choices and the simplest ways to integrate them with your current JiraAgent (optional, opt-in).

Recommendations
- Claude (Anthropic):
  - Strengths: Excellent summarization, long-context reasoning, safer defaults.
  - Use cases: Summarize issue threads, propose JQL, triage duplicates, draft responses.
  - Integration: VS Code extension for workflow; optional server route calling Anthropic Messages API.
- OpenAI (GPT family):
  - Strengths: Broad capabilities, strong coding assistance, versatile tools.
  - Use cases: Generate reports, suggest assignee routing, create dashboards.
  - Integration: Minimal Python client; cache prompts; rate limit and redact sensitive data.
- Local LLM (Llama/DeepSeek via Ollama):
  - Strengths: On-prem privacy, no external calls.
  - Trade-offs: Weaker quality vs frontier models; tune prompts carefully.
  - Integration: Run Ollama; call local HTTP endpoint for summaries/classification.

Best-fit by need
- Summarization of long Jira threads: Claude excels.
- Structured extraction (statuses, owners, timelines): GPT models are strong; add function-calling schema.
- On-prem constraints: Local LLM via Ollama; consider hybrid (local first, cloud fallback).

Integration patterns
- Optional backend endpoint:
  - Add `/ai/summarize` and `/ai/jql-suggest` in mcp-server; guard with env `AI_PROVIDER` and `AI_API_KEY`.
  - Redact PII; log minimal metadata; cache recent calls.
- VS Code-first:
  - Install the Claude extension for day-to-day triage and drafting without changing server code.
- Prompt hygiene:
  - Provide issue JSON (key, status, summary, latest comments, components).
  - Ask for concise outputs (bulleted summary, risk level, next action, suggested JQL).

Privacy and governance
- On-prem: Prefer local models or an internal proxy if external APIs are restricted.
- Redaction: Strip emails/usernames when sending to cloud LLMs unless allowed.
- Rate limits: Batch operations; set max token caps; add retries and circuit breakers.

If you want, I can:
- Add an optional `/ai/summarize` route with Anthropic/OpenAI today.
- Or set up a local Ollama integration for on-prem-only use.

marieswari-palanimarimuthu_verizon: Currently we are running html file directly. How can we host our project in any server and run it through any server

GitHub Copilot: Acknowledged. Plan: outline simple hosting options and give quick, copyable commands. If you want, I can also wire the Python MCP server to serve the UI.

Options to host the UI

- Python static server (quickest)
  - From ui:
  - PowerShell:
    ```powershell
    # Python 3
    python -m http.server 8080
    ```
  - Open `http://127.0.0.1:8080/index.html`.

- Host via the MCP Python server (serve UI + APIs together)
  - Add a static file handler in mcp-server to serve index.html and assets under `/`.
  - Benefits: Same origin, no CORS issues; UI talks to `/jira/...` directly.
  - I can implement this in the server: copy the UI into `mcp-server/static/` and add routes `/` → index.html, `/static/*` → files.

- IIS on Windows (built-in)
  - Enable IIS (Windows Features), add a site pointing to ui.
  - Set bindings to `http://localhost:8080` or your preferred port.
  - Place index.html in the site root.

- NGINX (production-grade)
  - Install NGINX; configure a server block to serve ui and reverse-proxy `/jira/*` to `http://127.0.0.1:8765`.
  - Useful to avoid CORS and unify domains.

- Node serve (if you have Node)
  - From ui:
    ```powershell
    npx serve -p 8080
    ```
  - Open `http://127.0.0.1:8080`.

Recommended setup (unified)
- Serve the UI from the MCP server to avoid CORS and keep things simple.
- Next steps I can do for you:
  - Add a `static` folder in mcp-server.
  - Route `/` to index.html; `/static/*` to assets.
  - Keep existing `/jira/*` endpoints.
- Then run:
  ```powershell
  $env:JIRA_BASE_URL='https://onejira.verizon.com'; $env:JIRA_API_VERSION='2'; $env:JIRA_USERNAME='<your_username>'; $env:JIRA_API_TOKEN='<your_password>'; $env:JIRA_MOCK='0'; python -m mcp_server
  ```

Thanks — I’ve implemented the server-side update flow and wired the UI to persist changes to Jira.

What I added

- Server (__main__.py)
  - `GET /jira/fields`: returns a map of field names → field IDs (used to resolve “Work Owner VCG” customfield).
  - `GET /jira/project-components?projectKey=...`: returns the project’s components (name/id).
  - `POST /jira/update`: accepts `{ key, components: [names], workOwnerVCG: '...', projectKey: '...' }`, resolves component names → IDs, looks up the customfield ID for “Work Owner VCG”, and updates the issue using Jira’s REST API (`PUT /rest/api/{2|3}/issue/{key}`).

- UI (index.html)
  - Removed default-tag UI and code.
  - “Update Selected” popup now calls `POST /jira/update` for each selected defect with:
    - `projectKey`: current selected project (e.g., `CXPOPER` as you specified).
    - `components`: comma-separated names parsed into an array.
    - `workOwnerVCG`: optional string.
  - After responses, the UI optimistically updates and highlights changed rows; shows any failures in an alert.

Usage

- Set Project to `CXPOPER` (or use custom).
- Select rows in the results table.
- Click “Update Selected”, enter components (comma-separated) and/or Work Owner VCG, click Apply.
- The UI will:
  - Persist updates to Jira via the server.
  - Update the table and highlight changed rows.
  - Show errors for any items that failed.

Notes and assumptions

- Work Owner VCG: The server discovers the customfield ID by name via `/field` and uses it in the patch; no manual ID needed.
- Components: Names are resolved to IDs via `/project/{key}/components`. If a name isn’t found in that project, it’s skipped for the update.

Next improvements (optional)
- After successful updates, re-fetch the specific issues to confirm the latest values from Jira.
- Add a toast banner for success/failure instead of alerts.
- Cache field maps and components per project to reduce API calls.

If you want, I can add a “Refresh Selected” button to re-pull the updated issues from Jira and confirm the changes in the UI immediately.

Made changes.

Thanks for the log. A 500 on POST `/jira/update` means the server-side update encountered an error. I’ve improved error handling to return clear reasons and added server logs.

What I changed
- Server `update_issue_fields` now:
  - Returns 400 with a message if component names can’t be resolved to IDs for the given project.
  - Returns 400 if the “Work Owner VCG” field ID can’t be found via `/field`.
  - Logs Jira HTTP errors and returns the exact error body.
  - Catches unexpected exceptions and returns a 500 with details.

How to diagnose quickly
- Try these helper endpoints to verify inputs:
  - List fields to confirm the custom field exists:
    - `GET http://127.0.0.1:8765/jira/fields`
  - List project components for `CXPOPER`:
    - `GET http://127.0.0.1:8765/jira/project-components?projectKey=CXPOPER`
- Then retry the update and check the server terminal; it will print any Jira error body.

Common causes
- Component names not in project `CXPOPER`: ensure the names you entered match exactly (case-sensitive).
- “Work Owner VCG” custom field isn’t named exactly that, or your account lacks edit permission for that field.
- Jira auth or permission issue for editing components/custom fields.

GitHub Copilot: You can check them in two quick ways:

- Browser: Open these URLs directly.
  - `http://127.0.0.1:8765/jira/fields`
  - `http://127.0.0.1:8765/jira/project-components?projectKey=CXPOPER`

- PowerShell: Use `Invoke-WebRequest` to see JSON quickly.
```powershell
Invoke-WebRequest -Uri "http://127.0.0.1:8765/jira/fields" | Select-Object -ExpandProperty Content
Invoke-WebRequest -Uri "http://127.0.0.1:8765/jira/project-components?projectKey=CXPOPER" | Select-Object -ExpandProperty Content
```

You’re checking for:
- Fields: Ensure there’s an entry where the name equals “Work Owner VCG” and note its `id` (e.g., `customfield_12345`).
- Components: Confirm the array lists components for `CXPOPER` with the exact `name` strings you plan to set (these get resolved to `id`s during update).

What happened:
- Your UI sent `projectKeyHint='B6VV_CXP Operations'`, which is not a Jira project key. The resolver calls `/project/{projectKey}/components`; with an invalid key, Jira returns an error that bubbled up to a 500.
- Also, `components=['PCT138 - CJCM Architecture']` is a name, not an ID. Name-matching can fail; IDs are reliable.

Plan: fix server JQL for multi-assignees (CJCM), add Status “All” behavior, tighten alignment/borders, and adjust CJCM label text.

- Server JQL: Proper multi-assignee support
  - Added CSV/CJCM parsing in __main__.py:
    - `assignedTo="__cjcm__:A, B, C"` → `assignee IN ("A", "B", "C")`
    - `assignedTo="A, B, C"` (general CSV) → `assignee IN ("A", "B", "C")`
    - `me`/`currentUser` → `assignee = currentUser()`
  - File: __main__.py, function `_build_jql` updated.

- UI: Status “All” + group borders
  - Status options now include `All`. When selected, status filter is omitted from JQL.
  - “All” is mutually exclusive with other status checkboxes.
  - Added subtle border/padding around Status/Priority groups for better alignment.
  - Files: index.html

Customer to activate an iPhone 16 plus.  The new phone is showing \"SOS\" and they could not get the verification text message to their phone number Order Number-->831352 Location Code -->1005001 *Cart ID :* 781cd9' for field 'text' is not valid: probably your range query is incorrect."],"errors":{}}


GitHub Copilot: Now hardening the JQL sanitization to prevent 400s when descriptions contain special characters.

Using "Apply Patch"

Thanks for the exact error text — that helped pinpoint it.

Cause
- Jira’s JQL text search uses Lucene syntax; raw descriptions often contain reserved characters and constructs like `[~username]`, quotes, asterisks, colons, etc. Even inside quotes, some sequences can break the parser, producing 400s.

Fix implemented
- Server __main__.py:
  - Escapes JQL string literals for quotes and backslashes.
  - Tokenizes the description/comments into safe alphanumeric words, filters short/numeric-only tokens, deduplicates, and limits to a small set.
  - Builds a safe JQL like:
    - `((text ~ "token1" OR text ~ "token2" ...) OR (comment ~ "token1" OR comment ~ "token2" ...))`
  - Falls back to summary tokens if description/comments yield none, and ultimately to `key = "<issue_key>"` if necessary.
  - Keeps the projects clause as `(project=A OR project=B OR ...)` wrapped with parentheses, then ANDs the token clause.

What to do next
- Restart the server to apply the changes:
```powershell
cd "C:\Users\v776133\Downloads\JiraAgent\mcp-server"
python -m mcp_server
```
- Open an issue in the details modal and click “Find Similar in 4 Projects”.

If any specific descriptions still cause errors, share the resulting JQL string and I’ll refine tokenization rules (e.g., increase token length threshold, exclude specific problematic words).

What I changed

Why this helps
- Requiring multiple tokens simultaneously (AND) increases relevance and reduces broad matches.

What’s new
- Server (__main__.py)
  - `GET /confluence/summarize?key=&space=&limit=`: Searches Confluence using tokens from the defect’s summary/description, fetches each page’s storage HTML, strips to text, and returns a concise extractive summary plus the list of matched pages. Includes `cql` for transparency.
  - Helpers:
    - `_html_to_text(html)`: Strips tags, scripts/styles, normalizes whitespace.
    - `_summarize_text(text, tokens)`: Simple sentence scoring by query-token hits to produce a short summary.

- Client (index.html)
  - Confluence panel in the details modal now includes a “Summarize” button.
  - Clicking “Summarize” calls `/confluence/summarize` using the current defect key and optional space, shows:

Thanks — the CQL you shared shows a single long phrase, which often yields no hits. I’ve updated the summarize logic to build more effective CQL and added a fallback so results are more likely.

What I changed
- Summarize CQL construction now uses tokens from the defect’s summary/description:
  - Primary query: AND across 2–4 tokens for both `text ~` and `title ~`, combined with OR:
    - `((text ~ "tok1" AND text ~ "tok2" ...) OR (title ~ "tok1" AND title ~ "tok2" ...))`
  - Fallback if no pages found: OR across tokens:
    - `((text ~ "tok1" OR text ~ "tok2" ...) OR (title ~ "tok1" OR title ~ "tok2" ...))`
- Space scoping remains `space = "PEG1"` if provided or configured.
- Summarization still blends headings/bullets and boosts sentences with phrases from Jira comments.

Next steps to try
- In the details modal, click “Summarize” again. The UI shows the CQL used; you should see multiple token clauses instead of a single long phrase.
- If it still shows “No pages,” try:
  - Setting `space` to `PEG1` (case-sensitive).
  - A simpler defect where tokens are common across pages.
  - Removing `space` (leave blank) to allow searching across all accessible spaces.

- Include page labels in the search (`label = "..."`) if you have known labels (e.g., activation, orders).
- Add `type = page` explicitly to the fallback query.
- Add a small toggle in the UI to switch between “strict” (AND) and “broad” (OR) search modes for Confluence.

marieswari-palanimarimuthu_verizon: May i know how could i do root cause analysis for the selected defect using old defects comment, current defect comments and confluence.

GitHub Copilot: Great question. Here’s a practical, repeatable workflow you can use in the UI now and how we can enhance it for deeper root cause analysis.

**Workflow**
- Collect Evidence: Open the defect details. Review summary, description, and all comments. Use “Summarize” in the Confluence panel to consolidate related pages into a quick brief.
- Find Prior Art: Use “Find Similar in 4 Projects” with strict mode to surface old, related defects. Read their comments and resolutions.
- Extract Signals: Identify recurring entities and patterns:
  - Components, modules, services, environments, versions, timestamps.
  - Error signatures, exception types, API endpoints, requests/responses.
  - Operational events in Confluence (deployments, config changes, known issues).
- Map Dependencies: From comments and Confluence pages, note upstream/downstream systems and interfaces. Pay attention to hand-offs and boundary failures.
- Build Hypotheses: Based on repeated patterns and timelines:
  - Configuration drift vs code regression vs data irregularity vs infra/network.
  - Change correlation: link defect creation/resurfacing to recent releases or changes documented in Confluence.
- Test Hypotheses: Look for confirmatory/contradictory evidence in:
  - Old defects with similar error strings.
  - Confluence incident runbooks or postmortems.
  - Version notes and deployment records.
- Conclude RCA: Capture the most likely cause, contributing factors, and recommended preventive actions (fix, guardrail, alert, doc change).

**Use the App Features**
- Strict Similar: Toggle “Strict mode” to require overlap of key tokens in summary/description; reduces noise and speeds pattern recognition.
- Confluence Summarize: Use the “Summarize” button to get a blended summary of headings, bullets, and relevant text, boosted by phrases found in the defect’s comments.
- Copy/Attach: Copy the summary for your RCA notes or “Attach to Jira” to share with the team directly on the defect.

**What I can add to make RCA faster**
- Keyword Extraction:
  - Tokens for errors, stack traces, endpoints, and config keys from comments and description.
  - Auto-highlight these tokens in similar defects and Confluence preview.
- Timeline View:
  - Show defect creation, updates, and comments next to Confluence change logs to visualize correlations.
- Entity Linking:
  - Link components and services to Confluence pages and known-issue trackers using labels or glossary mappings.
- Signals Heatmap:
  - Count frequency of recurring phrases across past defects and Confluence to spotlight dominant signals.
- Evidence Pack:
  - Generate a structured RCA draft: “Symptoms,” “Scope,” “Signals,” “Suspected Cause,” “Evidence,” “Fix,” “Preventive Actions,” and optionally attach it to Jira.

If you want, I can implement:
- Strict vs Broad toggles for Confluence search/summarize.
- Auto-highlighting of error signatures and endpoints across comments, similar defects, and Confluence pages.
- An “RCA Draft” panel in the modal that compiles the summary, similar defect snippets, and key Confluence bullets, ready to copy or attach.
